You see, there are two things that are true for comedians, in way over 90% of the cases. Almost each and every comedian is an outstanding actor overall looking and judging. They can act practically each serious role! But this is where the catch comes. After becoming a successful comedian, and you stay successful for a period of time, all people get,already have formed, a very structural and solid image about you. And based on it,  it's extremely hard (in some cases, even impossible) for the audience to see you in a serious role. Especially if the change is sudden, not gradual. It's simply a fact of life, a cultural phenomenon, and the way our brain reacts.  After a period of time, and a series of roles, which must be chosen very methodically and carefully, a comedian actor can begin to be accepted by the viewers as a complete actor, who does all kinds of roles (which he is, to begin with. But remember, we are talking about the viewers' perspective) and does it really good.  And that's exactly the case with Chris Rock From being Chris Rock all his life, to suddenly become a detective who will deal with Jigsaw murderer?!? That's a very hard and tough pill to swallow, let alone digest it, no matter how great he portray the character! People expect Chris Rock to do a parody of Saw, not the real thing! That's why I can't expect a huge success and turnaround for Chris, and the franchise it self - which has lost its credibility for some period, big time! And having Samuel L. Jackson as a side-kick in it, the man for whom people won't be surprised to see him even in their own, old home videos... isn't a very strong injection that would help the movie!

According to director Darren Lynn Bousman, a trap consisting of someone getting their face cut off had to be cut from the film in order for it to receive an R rating from the MPAA.  Chris Rock is a fan of the "Saw" franchise and pitched the idea to Lionsgate. As a result, they made him one of the lead actors, a co-writer, and executive producer.  The first film in the series not to be released in October  In order to secure an R rating, the film had to be submitted to the MPAA 11 times. All other attempts resulted in a rating of NC-17.  The first "Saw" film to not utilize the annual October Blood Drive with advertised poster models.  Darren Lynn Bousman revealed that Detective Drury originally had a bigger role and a "horrific death scene", but they cut it out for being "too much".  Marisol Nichols' second horror film, following "Scream 2" (1997).   This is the third film in the franchise where the phrase "Game Over" is not used; the other films that do not include the phrase are "Saw V" (2008) and "Jigsaw" (2017).  William Schenk marks the fourth Jigsaw Killer that had a family member killed. It is revealed that John Kramer lost his son, Gideon, in "Saw IV" (2007); Mark Hoffman lost his sister, Angelina, in "Saw V" (2008); and Logan Nelson lost his wife, Christine, in "Jigsaw" (2017).  Even though a photo of Tobin Bell is shown in the film, the actor did not receive any credit.  Is the second film in the series to be framed at 2.35:1. The first film to be framed in 2.35:1 was Jigsaw (2017).  Darren Lynn Bousman revealed that he was very angry during the finger-skinning sequence, knowing that they lost so much of it to the whims of the MPAA. "You saw every finger break, every bone pop, every knuckle snap."  Darren Lynn Bousman wanted a subway tunnel, but he was told the logistics just weren't in the budget. He held his ground, and they eventually built a subway tunnel set to meet their needs. It's a tiny set that uses forced perspective to make things look bigger than they are  The previous working title was "The Organ Donor".  According to Chris Rock, two films that were the inspiration for this film are "Seven" (1995) and "48 Hrs." (1982). Chris Rock's first horror film.

Wow this really does not do the previous films justice and I can tell just from the preview.
OK, so I was really looking forward to this movie, especially due to having both Samual L. Jackson and Chris Rock in it - "you wanna play games mother fucker?" - however, I realised early on that it is a Chris Rock movie and had Samuel L. Jackson too, in a similar vien as to how suicide squad is a Will Smith movie, there was far too much comedy in the film for the dark subject, unfortunately when you have a movie with these actors in who are known for a phrase used or the comedy they are related to, it takes away the feel of the movie.  It would have worked better with 'unkowns' like the saw frachise.  It was great to see Cary Elwes in the original line up and Shawnee Smith who are known for other things but not at the top, A list celebrity status at the time which I think helped with the success of the first films.  With the two main actors, already there are expectations before watching in due to their previous work and those expectations were met but for the wrong reasons, it is almost taking the franchise into dark comedy in the way Bride of Chucky did for the Child's Play franchise which is great if that is what you're looking for.  There is nothing wrong with a spin off if done right, I mean, look at Frasier, then look at Joey!  I don't think a TV series would work for the franchise as the TV series can't go as graphic as the movies do.  I won't be watching the sequel if there is one, it took years for Chil'd Play to get back to being a serious horror and then it still failed.  I am not dissing the actors, they delivered a great performance, I think the writing should not have had the comedy elements in there and both actors mentioned can deliver dark, serious performances.
